Of course I had to unplug them for some reason and now they dont work again. I rebooted but it didnt help. I messed with the sound settings but didnt understand what i was doing so stopped. 

I have the speakers plugged into the front port of my lenovo now. 
Sound settings :

The bottom meter on the playback tab flutters, showing that the music is being read. The "show" drop down list says "applications"
The port drop down list on the output tab says the speakers are unavailable (everything is grayed out), everything is grayed out under analog output, and it says the headphones are plugged in (the output port in the lenovo front is for headphones. but i was using it with my speakers when it worked before). and all of that in the output tab was "showing all devices" in the bottom drop down list. 
I tried both analog stereo and duplex stereo in the configurations (not understanding the difference) but neither worked. 

can anyone help

### Post by sandyd on 2015-05-04
Hi, can you post the following:
1. Output from the following command```
aplay -l
```
2. Run alsamixer, Press F6, and select your sound card (Usually, there is HDMI, and another card, choose whatever doesn't say HDMI). Take a screenshot of that.

Also, have you checked the volume outputs in pavucontrol?
You can install pavucontrol by running
```

sudo apt-get install pavucontrol
```
and start it by either typing in "Pulse Audio Volume Control" or pavucontrol in the menu.

The proper sound card should be set as the default sound output, and not the fallback.

---

### Post by sandyd on 2015-05-04
Volume is muted

In alsamixer, go back to the page where you were.

When you get to the page, you will notice that the first column (Master) has red text at the bottom while others have yellow.

The column with red text at the bottom is the one that is currently selected.

Use the arrow keys to pull down the volume by a lot on Master, Headphones, and PCM.

After that's done, press the 'M' key on those columns.

---

### Post by Geoffrey_Arndt on 2015-05-04
The MM's at the bottom of each column mean that "Mute" is enabled.    The normal status (mute 0ff) are two zeros "00" instead of two "MM's".    So, you have to use the tab key (or arrow keys) to select each column, and when the column is selected, you just press the M key on the keyboard to unmute - - - do that with each column (also, the up arrow key will increase the volume level if it's not already up at the top of the column).

Just press escape key when done.

See this short video for a basic "how to" . . . as alsamixer hasn't changed much in years:

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wWmXG-e6yzI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wWmXG-e6yzI)

There are other ways to do this by the way . . . some distros (can't recall how Xubuntu does it) have sound settings or graphical mixer programs that allow for unmute, etc.  (although the specific technique is a bit different)

---

### Post by Southron on 2015-05-04
> **sandyd said:**
> Hi, can you post the following:

Also, have you checked the volume outputs in pavucontrol?
You can install pavucontrol by running
```

sudo apt-get install pavucontrol
```
and start it by either typing in "Pulse Audio Volume Control" or pavucontrol in the menu.

The proper sound card should be set as the default sound output, and not the fallback.

The settings I wrote about in the original post were from pavucontrol ( I didnt realize it until I searched for pauvcontrol after getting your directions). No sound card is listed in the output devices tab. The drop down list just says speakers (unavailable), Headphones (plugged in) and analog output as options
